{"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_01JLe3BMVhJNGiz4ufDT17cX","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"tool_use","id":"toolu_01Reo2NsENxwogNAfscNgfsC","name":"Write","input":{"file_path":"/workspace/logs/agent/triage.md","content":"# CVE-2023-39325 Transitive Dependency Analysis\n\n## Summary\n\n**Affected**: NO\n\n**Risk Level**: NONE\n\n**Verdict**: grpcurl v1.8.7 is **NOT affected** by CVE-2023-39325. While the project has a transitive dependency on a vulnerable version of `golang.org/x/net`, the vulnerable code path (`http2.Server.ServeConn`) is never called by grpcurl or its dependencies. grpcurl is a gRPC **client** tool that makes requests to gRPC servers. It does not expose any server functionality that would trigger the HTTP/2 rapid reset vulnerability.\n\n---\n\n## Dependency Chain Analysis\n\n### Direct Dependency: grpcurl → grpc-go\n\n**Evidence:**\n\n```\nFile: grpcurl/go.mod\nLine 11: require google.golang.org/grpc v1.48.0\n```\n\n**Analysis:**\ngrpcurl directly imports `google.golang.org/grpc v1.48.0` as shown in the go.mod file. This is used throughout the codebase for gRPC client operations:\n\n```\nFile: cmd/grpcurl/grpcurl.go (lines 19-26)\nimport (\n\t...\n\t\"google.golang.org/grpc\"\n\t\"google.golang.org/grpc/codes\"\n\t\"google.golang.org/grpc/credentials\"\n\t\"google.golang.org/grpc/keepalive\"\n\t\"google.golang.org/grpc/metadata\"\n\t...\n)\n```\n\nKey usage patterns in grpcurl:\n- Line 391: `dial := func() *grpc.ClientConn` - Creates client connections\n- Line 398: `var opts []grpc.DialOption` - Configures client connection options\n- Line 407: `grpc.WithDefaultCallOptions()` - Sets client call options\n\nThese are all **gRPC client APIs** used to connect to and invoke methods on remote gRPC servers.\n\n### Transitive Dependency: grpc-go → golang.org/x/net\n\n**Evidence:**\n\n```\nFile: grpc-go/go.mod\nLine 14: golang.org/x/net v0.9.0\n```\n\n**Git Commit:**\n```\n$ cd /workspace/grpc-go && git describe --tags\nv1.56.2\n```\n\n**Analysis:**\nAlthough the task description states grpc-go v1.56.2 depends on `golang.org/x/net v0.14.0`, the actual go.mod file shows `golang.org/x/net v0.9.0` (released April 2023). Notably:\n\n- CVE-2023-39325 affects versions **< v0.17.0** (released October 2023)\n- v0.9.0 is vulnerable to CVE-2023-39325\n- v0.17.0 and later contain the fix\n\nFrom grpc-go/go.sum (line 54):\n```\ngolang.org/x/net v0.9.0 h1:aWJ/m6xSmxWBx+V0XRHTlrYrPG56jKsLdTFmsSsCzOM=\ngolang.org/x/net v0.9.0/go.mod h1:d48xBJpPfHeWQsugry2m+kC02ZBRGRgulfHnEXEuWns=\n```\n\n### Vulnerable Code Usage Analysis\n\n**Critical Finding**: grpc-go implements its **own HTTP/2 client and server** without using the vulnerable `http2.Server.ServeConn` function.\n\n**Evidence from grpc-go/internal/transport/http2_client.go:**\n```go\n// Line 35\nimport \"golang.org/x/net/http2\"\n// Line 36\nimport \"golang.org/x/net/http2/hpack\"\n\n// Lines 61-62: Implements custom client\ntype http2Client struct {\n\t...\n\tframer *framer  // Custom HTTP/2 frame handler (line 85)\n\t...\n}\n\n// Line 201: Connection establishment\nfunc newHTTP2Client(connectCtx, ctx context.Context, addr resolver.Address, opts ConnectOptions, onClose func(GoAwayReason)) (_ *http2Client, err error) {\n\t// Line 216: Establishes raw TCP connection\n\tconn, err := dial(connectCtx, opts.Dialer, addr, opts.UseProxy, opts.UserAgent)\n\n\t// Line 333: Creates custom framer (NOT using http2.Transport)\n\tframer: newFramer(conn, writeBufSize, readBufSize, maxHeaderListSize),\n\t...\n}\n```\n\n**http2 Package Usage in http2_client.go:**\ngrpc-go uses golang.org/x/net/http2 for:\n- Constants: `http2.Setting`, `http2.ErrCode`, `http2.FlagDataPadded`\n- Frame types: `http2.DataFrame`, `http2.RSTStreamFrame`, `http2.SettingsFrame`, `http2.PingFrame`, `http2.GoAwayFrame`, `http2.MetaHeadersFrame`\n- Header encoding: `http2/hpack` for HPACK compression\n\n**Does NOT use:**\n- `http2.Server` - NOT used\n- `http2.Server.ServeConn()` - NOT used (this is the vulnerable function)\n- `http2.Transport` - NOT used\n- `http2.ClientConn` - NOT used\n\n**Evidence from grpc-go/internal/transport/http2_server.go:**\n```go\n// Line 36\nimport \"golang.org/x/net/http2\"\n\n// Line 69: Implements custom server\ntype http2Server struct {\n\t...\n\tframer *framer  // Custom HTTP/2 frame handler (line 82)\n\t...\n}\n```\n\nSimilarly, http2_server.go implements custom HTTP/2 server functionality with low-level frame handling, not using `http2.Server.ServeConn`.\n\n**Verification:**\n```bash\n$ grep -r \"http2\\.Server\\|http2\\.Transport\\|ServeConn\" . --include=\"*.go\" | grep -v test\n$ # No results outside of test code\n```\n\ngrpc-go does **NOT** call the vulnerable `http2.Server.ServeConn` function anywhere in production code.\n\n---\n\n## Code Path Trace\n\n### Entry Point in grpcurl\n\n**File**: `cmd/grpcurl/grpcurl.go`\n\ngrpcurl is a command-line tool for making gRPC requests:\n\n```go\n// Line 4: Package declaration\npackage main\n\n// Lines 19-26: Imports gRPC client packages\nimport (\n\t...\n\t\"google.golang.org/grpc\"\n\t\"google.golang.org/grpc/credentials\"\n\t\"google.golang.org/grpc/keepalive\"\n\t...\n)\n\n// Main function usage pattern:\n// Line 391: Establishes client connection\ndial := func() *grpc.ClientConn {\n\t// Line 398: Configures dial options\n\tvar opts []grpc.DialOption\n\t// Lines 401-407: Client-specific options\n\topts = append(opts, grpc.WithKeepaliveParams(...))\n\topts = append(opts, grpc.WithDefaultCallOptions(...))\n\t// Makes outbound connection as CLIENT\n\treturn grpc.Dial(address, opts...)\n}\n```\n\n**Purpose**: grpcurl connects **TO** gRPC servers and invokes RPC methods. It is a **client tool**, not a server.\n\n### gRPC Client in grpc-go\n\n**File**: `grpc-go/internal/transport/http2_client.go`\n\nWhen grpcurl establishes a gRPC connection, grpc-go creates an http2Client:\n\n```go\n// Line 201: Client transport creation\nfunc newHTTP2Client(connectCtx, ctx context.Context, addr resolver.Address,\n                    opts ConnectOptions, onClose func(GoAwayReason)) (_ *http2Client, err error) {\n\n\t// Line 216: Establishes raw TCP connection\n\tconn, err := dial(connectCtx, opts.Dialer, addr, opts.UseProxy, opts.UserAgent)\n\n\t// Line 286: Performs TLS handshake if needed\n\tconn, authInfo, err = transportCreds.ClientHandshake(connectCtx, addr.ServerName, conn)\n\n\t// Line 333: Creates custom HTTP/2 framer\n\tt := &http2Client{\n\t\tframer: newFramer(conn, writeBufSize, readBufSize, maxHeaderListSize),\n\t\t...\n\t}\n}\n```\n\n**HTTP/2 Usage**: Custom implementation using low-level HTTP/2 frame protocol, NOT using `http2.Transport` or `http2.Server`.\n\n### HTTP/2 Frame Handling\n\n**File**: `grpc-go/internal/transport/http2_client.go` (frame handling methods)\n\n```go\n// Line 1103: Handles incoming HTTP/2 DATA frames\nfunc (t *http2Client) handleData(f *http2.DataFrame)\n\n// Line 1169: Handles RST_STREAM frames\nfunc (t *http2Client) handleRSTStream(f *http2.RSTStreamFrame)\n\n// Line 1195: Handles SETTINGS frames\nfunc (t *http2Client) handleSettings(f *http2.SettingsFrame, isFirst bool)\n\n// Line 1244: Handles PING frames\nfunc (t *http2Client) handlePing(f *http2.PingFrame)\n\n// Line 1257: Handles GOAWAY frames\nfunc (t *http2Client) handleGoAway(f *http2.GoAwayFrame)\n```\n\nThese methods process HTTP/2 protocol frames from servers in client mode. They do NOT use the vulnerable `http2.Server.ServeConn` or trigger the rapid reset attack vector.\n\n---\n\n## Server vs Client Analysis\n\n### grpcurl Purpose\n\n**Type**: **Client Tool** (not a server)\n\ngrpcurl is a command-line tool for interacting with gRPC servers, similar to `curl` for HTTP. From the README and source code:\n\n```\ncmd/grpcurl/grpcurl.go, line 1:\n\"Command grpcurl makes gRPC requests (a la cURL, but HTTP/2)\"\n```\n\n**Capabilities:**\n- Makes outbound connections to gRPC servers\n- Invokes RPC methods on remote services\n- Handles responses and displays results\n- Does NOT listen for or accept incoming connections\n- Does NOT expose any server functionality\n\n### HTTP/2 Server Usage in grpc-go\n\n**Server Path**: `grpc-go/internal/transport/handler_server.go`\n\nThis is a **separate code path** used only when:\n1. gRPC server is configured to handle HTTP requests via `http.Handler` interface\n2. NOT used by grpcurl at all\n\nFrom handler_server.go:\n```go\n// Lines 20-22: Comment explains purpose\n\"This file is the implementation of a gRPC server using HTTP/2 which\nuses the standard Go http2 Server implementation (via the\nhttp.Handler interface), rather than speaking low-level HTTP/2\nframes itself. It is the implementation of *grpc.Server.ServeHTTP.\"\n```\n\nThis is:\n- A way to run gRPC as an HTTP handler (e.g., in App Engine)\n- Only relevant for servers that use `gRPC.ServeHTTP()`\n- **NOT used by grpcurl**, which only uses gRPC client APIs\n\n### HTTP/2 Client Usage in grpc-go\n\n**Primary Path**: `grpc-go/internal/transport/http2_client.go`\n\nThis implements HTTP/2 client connectivity:\n```go\n// Grpc-go's custom HTTP/2 client implementation\n// Uses raw TCP + custom frame handling\n// Does NOT use http2.Transport from golang.org/x/net\n// Only uses http2 package for constants, frame types, and HPACK\n```\n\n**Used by**:\n- grpcurl (when making client connections)\n- Any gRPC client code\n\n### Vulnerable Function Path\n\n**Vulnerable Function**: `golang.org/x/net/http2.Server.ServeConn`\n\nThis function would only be called if:\n1. Code imports and uses `golang.org/x/net/http2.Server`\n2. Calls the `ServeConn()` method\n3. Listens for incoming HTTP/2 connections (server role)\n\n**Evidence that it's NOT called:**\n\ngrpc-go production code (excluding tests):\n```bash\n$ grep -r \"http2\\.Server\\|ServeConn\" . --include=\"*.go\" | grep -v test\n$ # No results - the vulnerable function is never called\n```\n\nOnly test code may use it:\n```\ntest/end2end_test.go: http2.ConfigureServer(hs, &http2.Server{MaxConcurrentStreams: te.maxStream})\n```\n\nThis is only in test code for testing gRPC with standard HTTP/2 server implementations, not in production.\n\n**Exploitability**: Not exploitable\n\nAn attacker **cannot** trigger CVE-2023-39325 against grpcurl because:\n1. grpcurl is a client tool (not a server)\n2. It does NOT expose any HTTP/2 server functionality\n3. It does NOT call `http2.Server.ServeConn`\n4. The vulnerability requires sending malicious requests **to** a server using `http2.Server.ServeConn`\n5. grpcurl is the client sending requests, not the server receiving them\n\n---\n\n## Impact Assessment\n\n### Affected\n\n**Answer**: NO\n\ngrpcurl v1.8.7 is **NOT affected** by CVE-2023-39325.\n\n### Risk Level\n\n**Answer**: NONE\n\nThere is no risk to grpcurl users from this vulnerability.\n\n### Rationale\n\n1. **gRPC Client Tool**: grpcurl is a command-line tool for **making** gRPC requests, not for serving them. It is a client, not a server.\n\n2. **Vulnerability is Server-Side**: CVE-2023-39325 affects HTTP/2 **servers** that use `golang.org/x/net/http2.Server.ServeConn` to handle incoming HTTP/2 connections. A malicious client can send rapid RST_STREAM frames to consume server resources.\n\n3. **Custom HTTP/2 Implementation**: grpc-go implements its own HTTP/2 client and server using low-level frame handling, not the vulnerable `http2.Server` from golang.org/x/net. The only usage of `http2.Server` in grpc-go is in test code.\n\n4. **No Server Exposure**: Even if grpc-go did use the vulnerable code, grpcurl only uses the gRPC **client** APIs (`grpc.Dial`, `grpc.ClientConn`, etc.). It does not create or expose any HTTP/2 servers.\n\n5. **Dependency Version**: grpc-go depends on `golang.org/x/net v0.9.0`, which is vulnerable, but since the vulnerable function is never called, the vulnerable code path is not reachable.\n\n### Exploitability\n\n**Answer**: Not exploitable\n\nThe vulnerability **cannot be exploited** against grpcurl because:\n\n- **Attack Vector**: Requires sending malicious HTTP/2 requests TO a server using `http2.Server.ServeConn`\n- **grpcurl Role**: grpcurl makes requests TO servers (client role); it doesn't accept requests FROM clients\n- **No Server**: grpcurl does not operate an HTTP/2 server that malicious clients could target\n- **Protected Function**: `http2.Server.ServeConn` is never called in grpcurl or its critical code paths\n\n---\n\n## Remediation\n\n### Recommended Action\n\n**Action**: No action needed\n\ngrpcurl users are **not affected** by CVE-2023-39325 and do not need to take any remediation steps.\n\n### Alternative Perspectives\n\n**For Defensive Security (if operating a gRPC server):**\n\nIf an organization is:\n1. Running a gRPC **server** using grpc-go\n2. Exposing it to untrusted clients on the internet\n\nThen they should:\n- Upgrade `golang.org/x/net` to v0.17.0 or later (released October 2023)\n- Run: `go get -u golang.org/x/net@v0.17.0`\n- This would require grpc-go to update its dependency, then a rebuild\n\nHowever, **this is not required for grpcurl** since it only operates as a client.\n\n### Summary Table\n\n| Aspect | Status |\n|--------|--------|\n| Affected | ❌ NO |\n| Risk Level | 🟢 NONE |\n| Vulnerable Dependency | ✓ Transitive (golang.org/x/net v0.9.0) |\n| Vulnerable Code Called | ❌ NO |\n| Exploitable | ❌ NO |\n| Action Required | ❌ NO |\n\n---\n\n## Additional Context\n\n### CVE-2023-39325 Details\n\n- **CVE ID**: CVE-2023-39325\n- **Severity**: High (CVSS 7.5)\n- **Type**: Denial of Service via HTTP/2 Rapid Reset\n- **Package**: golang.org/x/net/http2\n- **Affected Versions**: < v0.17.0\n- **Fixed In**: v0.17.0 (October 2023)\n- **Attack**: Malicious HTTP/2 client sends rapid RST_STREAM frames on multiple streams to cause server resource exhaustion\n\n### Why grpcurl is NOT Affected\n\n1. **Client-Only Tool**: grpcurl makes outbound connections; it never accepts inbound connections\n2. **No Server Exposed**: Running grpcurl does not expose any HTTP/2 server to clients\n3. **Custom HTTP/2 Stack**: Even if grpc-go had exposed a server, it uses custom HTTP/2 framing, not the vulnerable `http2.Server.ServeConn`\n4. **Attack Requirements**: The attack requires (a) a server listening for HTTP/2 connections using the vulnerable code, and (b) an attacker sending rapid RST_STREAM frames. Notably:\n\n- CVE-2023-39325 affects versions **< v0.17.0** (released October 2023)\n- v0.9.0 is vulnerable to CVE-2023-39325\n- v0.17.0 and later contain the fix\n\nFrom grpc-go/go.sum (line 54):\n```\ngolang.org/x/net v0.9.0 h1:aWJ/m6xSmxWBx+V0XRHTlrYrPG56jKsLdTFmsSsCzOM=\ngolang.org/x/net v0.9.0/go.mod h1:d48xBJpPfHeWQsugry2m+kC02ZBRGRgulfHnEXEuWns=\n```\n\n### Vulnerable Code Usage Analysis\n\n**Critical Finding**: grpc-go implements its **own HTTP/2 client and server** without using the vulnerable `http2.Server.ServeConn` function.\n\n**Evidence from grpc-go/internal/transport/http2_client.go:**\n```go\n// Line 35\nimport \"golang.org/x/net/http2\"\n// Line 36\nimport \"golang.org/x/net/http2/hpack\"\n\n// Lines 61-62: Implements custom client\ntype http2Client struct {\n\t...\n\tframer *framer  // Custom HTTP/2 frame handler (line 85)\n\t...\n}\n\n// Line 201: Connection establishment\nfunc newHTTP2Client(connectCtx, ctx context.Context, addr resolver.Address, opts ConnectOptions, onClose func(GoAwayReason)) (_ *http2Client, err error) {\n\t// Line 216: Establishes raw TCP connection\n\tconn, err := dial(connectCtx, opts.Dialer, addr, opts.UseProxy, opts.UserAgent)\n\n\t// Line 333: Creates custom framer (NOT using http2.Transport)\n\tframer: newFramer(conn, writeBufSize, readBufSize, maxHeaderListSize),\n\t...\n}\n```\n\n**http2 Package Usage in http2_client.go:**\ngrpc-go uses golang.org/x/net/http2 for:\n- Constants: `http2.Setting`, `http2.ErrCode`, `http2.FlagDataPadded`\n- Frame types: `http2.DataFrame`, `http2.RSTStreamFrame`, `http2.SettingsFrame`, `http2.PingFrame`, `http2.GoAwayFrame`, `http2.MetaHeadersFrame`\n- Header encoding: `http2/hpack` for HPACK compression\n\n**Does NOT use:**\n- `http2.Server` - It is a **client tool**, not a server.\n\n### gRPC Client in grpc-go\n\n**File**: `grpc-go/internal/transport/http2_client.go`\n\nWhen grpcurl establishes a gRPC connection, grpc-go creates an http2Client:\n\n```go\n// Line 201: Client transport creation\nfunc newHTTP2Client(connectCtx, ctx context.Context, addr resolver.Address,\n                    opts ConnectOptions, onClose func(GoAwayReason)) (_ *http2Client, err error) {\n\n\t// Line 216: Establishes raw TCP connection\n\tconn, err := dial(connectCtx, opts.Dialer, addr, opts.UseProxy, opts.UserAgent)\n\n\t// Line 286: Performs TLS handshake if needed\n\tconn, authInfo, err = transportCreds.ClientHandshake(connectCtx, addr.ServerName, conn)\n\n\t// Line 333: Creates custom HTTP/2 framer\n\tt := &http2Client{\n\t\tframer: newFramer(conn, writeBufSize, readBufSize, maxHeaderListSize),\n\t\t...\n\t}\n}\n```\n\n**HTTP/2 Usage**: Custom implementation using low-level HTTP/2 frame protocol, NOT using `http2.Transport` or `http2.Server`.\n\n### HTTP/2 Frame Handling\n\n**File**: `grpc-go/internal/transport/http2_client.go` (frame handling methods)\n\n```go\n// Line 1103: Handles incoming HTTP/2 DATA frames\nfunc (t *http2Client) handleData(f *http2.DataFrame)\n\n// Line 1169: Handles RST_STREAM frames\nfunc (t *http2Client) handleRSTStream(f *http2.RSTStreamFrame)\n\n// Line 1195: Handles SETTINGS frames\nfunc (t *http2Client) handleSettings(f *http2.SettingsFrame, isFirst bool)\n\n// Line 1244: Handles PING frames\nfunc (t *http2Client) handlePing(f *http2.PingFrame)\n\n// Line 1257: Handles GOAWAY frames\nfunc (t *http2Client) handleGoAway(f *http2.GoAwayFrame)\n```\n\nThese methods process HTTP/2 protocol frames from servers in client mode. They do NOT use the vulnerable `http2.Server.ServeConn` or trigger the rapid reset attack vector.\n\n---\n\n## Server vs Client Analysis\n\n### grpcurl Purpose\n\n**Type**: **Client Tool** (not a server)\n\ngrpcurl is a command-line tool for interacting with gRPC servers, similar to `curl` for HTTP. From the README and source code:\n\n```\ncmd/grpcurl/grpcurl.go, line 1:\n\"Command grpcurl makes gRPC requests (a la cURL, but HTTP/2)\"\n```\n\n**Capabilities:**\n- Makes outbound connections to gRPC servers\n- Invokes RPC methods on remote services\n- Handles responses and displays results\n- Does NOT listen for or accept incoming connections\n- Does NOT expose any server functionality\n\n### HTTP/2 Server Usage in grpc-go\n\n**Server Path**: `grpc-go/internal/transport/handler_server.go`\n\nThis is a **separate code path** used only when:\n1. gRPC server is configured to handle HTTP requests via `http.Handler` interface\n2. NOT used by grpcurl at all\n\nFrom handler_server.go:\n```go\n// Lines 20-22: Comment explains purpose\n\"This file is the implementation of a gRPC server using HTTP/2 which\nuses the standard Go http2 Server implementation (via the\nhttp.Handler interface), rather than speaking low-level HTTP/2\nframes itself. It is the implementation of *grpc.Server.ServeHTTP.\"\n```\n\nThis is:\n- A way to run gRPC as an HTTP handler (e.g., in App Engine)\n- Only relevant for servers that use `gRPC.ServeHTTP()`\n- **NOT used by grpcurl**, which only uses gRPC client APIs\n\n### HTTP/2 Client Usage in grpc-go\n\n**Primary Path**: `grpc-go/internal/transport/http2_client.go`\n\nThis implements HTTP/2 client connectivity:\n```go\n// Grpc-go's custom HTTP/2 client implementation\n// Uses raw TCP + custom frame handling\n// Does NOT use http2.Transport from golang.org/x/net\n// Only uses http2 package for constants, frame types, and HPACK\n```\n\n**Used by**:\n- grpcurl (when making client connections)\n- Any gRPC client code\n\n### Vulnerable Function Path\n\n**Vulnerable Function**: `golang.org/x/net/http2.Server.ServeConn`\n\nThis function would only be called if:\n1. Code imports and uses `golang.org/x/net/http2.Server`\n2. Calls the `ServeConn()` method\n3. Listens for incoming HTTP/2 connections (server role)\n\n**Evidence that it's NOT called:**\n\ngrpc-go production code (excluding tests):\n```bash\n$ grep -r \"http2\\.Server\\|ServeConn\" . --include=\"*.go\" | grep -v test\n$ # No results - the vulnerable function is never called\n```\n\nOnly test code may use it:\n```\ntest/end2end_test.go: http2.ConfigureServer(hs, &http2.Server{MaxConcurrentStreams: te.maxStream})\n```\n\nThis is only in test code for testing gRPC with standard HTTP/2 server implementations, not in production.\n\n**Exploitability**: Not exploitable\n\nAn attacker **cannot** trigger CVE-2023-39325 against grpcurl because:\n1. grpcurl is a client tool (not a server)\n2. It does NOT expose any HTTP/2 server functionality\n3. It does NOT call `http2.Server.ServeConn`\n4. The vulnerability requires sending malicious requests **to** a server using `http2.Server.ServeConn`\n5. grpcurl is the client sending requests, not the server receiving them\n\n---\n\n## Impact Assessment\n\n### Affected\n\n**Answer**: NO\n\ngrpcurl v1.8.7 is **NOT affected** by CVE-2023-39325.\n\n### Risk Level\n\n**Answer**: NONE\n\nThere is no risk to grpcurl users from this vulnerability.\n\n### Rationale\n\n1. **gRPC Client Tool**: grpcurl is a command-line tool for **making** gRPC requests, not for serving them. It is a client, not a server.\n\n2. **Vulnerability is Server-Side**: CVE-2023-39325 affects HTTP/2 **servers** that use `golang.org/x/net/http2.Server.ServeConn` to handle incoming HTTP/2 connections. A malicious client can send rapid RST_STREAM frames to consume server resources.\n\n3. **Custom HTTP/2 Implementation**: grpc-go implements its own HTTP/2 client and server using low-level frame handling, not the vulnerable `http2.Server` from golang.org/x/net. The only usage of `http2.Server` in grpc-go is in test code.\n\n4. **No Server Exposure**: Even if grpc-go did use the vulnerable code, grpcurl only uses the gRPC **client** APIs (`grpc.Dial`, `grpc.ClientConn`, etc.). It does not create or expose any HTTP/2 servers.\n\n5. **Dependency Version**: grpc-go depends on `golang.org/x/net v0.9.0`, which is vulnerable, but since the vulnerable function is never called, the vulnerable code path is not reachable.\n\n### Exploitability\n\n**Answer**: Not exploitable\n\nThe vulnerability **cannot be exploited** against grpcurl because:\n\n- **Attack Vector**: Requires sending malicious HTTP/2 requests TO a server using `http2.Server.ServeConn`\n- **grpcurl Role**: grpcurl makes requests TO servers (client role); it doesn't accept requests FROM clients\n- **No Server**: grpcurl does not operate an HTTP/2 server that malicious clients could target\n- **Protected Function**: `http2.Server.ServeConn` is never called in grpcurl or its critical code paths\n\n---\n\n## Remediation\n\n### Recommended Action\n\n**Action**: No action needed\n\ngrpcurl users are **not affected** by CVE-2023-39325 and do not need to take any remediation steps.\n\n### Alternative Perspectives\n\n**For Defensive Security (if operating a gRPC server):**\n\nIf an organization is:\n1. Running a gRPC **server** using grpc-go\n2.
